	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">City of Bradford</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>

For the municipal borough, designated a city in 1897, see <a href="/wiki/Bradford" title="Bradford">Bradford</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Bradford_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Bradford (disambiguation)">Bradford (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p>The <b>City of Bradford</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-Bradford.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/33/En-uk-Bradford.ogg" class="internal" title="En-uk-Bradford.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_England" title="Local government in England">local government district</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a>, England, with the status of a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_borough" title="Metropolitan borough">metropolitan borough</a>. It is named after its largest settlement, <a href="/wiki/Bradford" title="Bradford">Bradford</a>, but covers a far larger area which includes the towns of <a href="/wiki/Keighley" title="Keighley">Keighley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shipley,_West_Yorkshire" title="Shipley, West Yorkshire">Shipley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bingley" title="Bingley">Bingley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilkley" title="Ilkley">Ilkley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haworth" title="Haworth">Haworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silsden" title="Silsden">Silsden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denholme" title="Denholme">Denholme</a>. Bradford has a population of 528,155,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_population" title="List of English districts by population">fourth-most populous</a> metropolitan district and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_population" title="List of English districts by population">sixth-most populous</a> local authority district in England. It forms part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Urban_Area" title="West Yorkshire Urban Area">West Yorkshire Urban Area</a> conurbation which in 2011 had a population of 1,777,934,<sup id="cite_ref-BUA_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUA-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and the city is part of the Leeds-Bradford Larger Urban Zone (LUZ), which, with a population of 2,393,300, is the fourth largest in the United Kingdom after London, Birmingham and Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city is situated on the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a>, and is bounded to the east by the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Leeds" title="City of Leeds">City of Leeds</a>, the south east by the Metropolitan Borough of <a href="/wiki/Kirklees" title="Kirklees">Kirklees</a> and the south west by the Metropolitan Borough of <a href="/wiki/Calderdale" title="Calderdale">Calderdale</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Pendle" title="Borough of Pendle">Pendle</a> borough of <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a> lies to the west, whilst the <a href="/wiki/Craven" title="Craven">Craven</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Harrogate" title="Borough of Harrogate">Harrogate</a> boroughs of <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a> lie to the north west and north east of the city. Bradford is the 4th largest metropolitan district in the country, and the contiguous urban area to the north which includes the towns of Shipley and Bingley is heavily populated. The <a href="/wiki/Spa_town" title="Spa town">spa town</a> of Ilkley lies further north, whilst the town of Keighley lies to the west. Roughly two thirds of the district is rural, with an environment varying from <a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorlands</a> in the north and west, to valleys and floodplains formed by the river systems that flow throughout the district. More than half of Bradford's land is green open space, stretching over part of the <a href="/wiki/Airedale" title="Airedale">Airedale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wharfedale" title="Wharfedale">Wharfedale</a> Valleys, across the hills and the Pennine moorland between. The <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Dales" title="Yorkshire Dales">Yorkshire Dales</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District</a> are both in close proximity.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The City of Bradford has architecture designated as being of special or historic importance, most of which were constructed with local stone, with 5,800 <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed buildings</a> and 59 <a href="/wiki/Conservation_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservation area">conservation areas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Model_village" title="Model village">model village</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saltaire" title="Saltaire">Saltaire</a> has been listed as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>. Central Bradford rose to prominence during the 19th century as an international centre of <a href="/wiki/Textile_manufacture_during_the_Industrial_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Textile manufacture during the Industrial Revolution">textile manufacture</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>. The area's access to a supply of coal, iron ore and soft water facilitated the growth of Bradford's manufacturing base, which, as textile manufacture grew, led to an explosion in population and was a stimulus to civic investment. However, Bradford has faced similar challenges to the rest of the post-industrial area of northern England, including deindustrialisation, housing problems, and economic deprivation. Wool and textiles still play an important part in the city's <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a>, but today's fastest-growing sectors include <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>, financial services, digital industries, environmental technologies, cultural industries, <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> and retail headquarters and distribution. Bradford's reputation as a base for high technology, scientific and computer-based industries is growing, building on a long tradition of innovation, high skill levels and quality products.
</p><p>Bradford has experienced significant levels of immigration throughout the 19th and 20th centuries. In the 1840s Bradford's population was significantly increased by migrants from Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> particularly <a href="/wiki/County_Mayo" title="County Mayo">rural Mayo</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_Sligo" title="County Sligo">Sligo</a>, and by 1851 around 18,000 people of Irish origin resided in the town, representing around 10% of the population, the largest proportion in <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>. Around the same time there was also an influx of  <a href="/wiki/German_Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="German Jewish">German Jewish migrants</a> to the town, and by 1910 around 1,500 people of German origin resided in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
In the 1950s there was large scale immigration from <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> and to a lesser extent from <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>. Bradford has the second highest proportion in <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a> outside <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, in terms of population (behind <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>) and in percentage (behind <a href="/wiki/Slough" title="Slough">Slough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_with_Darwen" title="Blackburn with Darwen">Blackburn with Darwen</a>). An estimated 140,149 people of <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a> origin reside in the city, representing around 26.83% of the city's population.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> An estimated 352,317 of all White ethnic groups reside in the city which includes people of Polish and Irish origin, representing around 67.44% of the city's population.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180922122344/http://observatory.bradford.gov.uk/dataviews/tabular?viewId=274&amp;geoId=6&amp;subsetId=">[5]</a>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bradford was granted the status of a city in 1897. Bradford was incorporated as a municipal borough in 1847, covering the parishes of Bradford, Horton and Manningham. It became a county borough with the passing of the Local Government Act 1888. The county borough was granted city status by <a href="/wiki/Letters_Patent" class="mw-redirect" title="Letters Patent">Letters Patent</a> in 1897.
</p><p>Bradford was expanded in 1882 to include Allerton, Bolton, Bowling, Heaton, Thornbury and Tyersall. In 1899 it was further expanded by adding North Bierley, Eccleshill, Idle, Thornton, Tong and Wyke. Clayton was added in 1930.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Bront%C3%AB_Sisters_by_Patrick_Branwell_Bront%C3%AB_restored.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/The_Bront%C3%AB_Sisters_by_Patrick_Branwell_Bront%C3%AB_restored.jpg/220px-The_Bront%C3%AB_Sisters_by_Patrick_Branwell_Bront%C3%AB_restored.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/The_Bront%C3%AB_Sisters_by_Patrick_Branwell_Bront%C3%AB_restored.jpg/330px-The_Bront%C3%AB_Sisters_by_Patrick_Branwell_Bront%C3%AB_restored.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/The_Bront%C3%AB_Sisters_by_Patrick_Branwell_Bront%C3%AB_restored.jpg/440px-The_Bront%C3%AB_Sisters_by_Patrick_Branwell_Bront%C3%AB_restored.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="2908" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Bront%C3%AB_Sisters_by_Patrick_Branwell_Bront%C3%AB_restored.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Anne_Bront%C3%AB" title="Anne Brontë">Anne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emily_Bront%C3%AB" title="Emily Brontë">Emily</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Bront%C3%AB" title="Charlotte Brontë">Charlotte</a> Brontë, by their brother <a href="/wiki/Branwell_Bront%C3%AB" title="Branwell Brontë">Branwell</a> (c.&#160;1834).</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bront%C3%AB_sisters" class="mw-redirect" title="Brontë sisters">The Brontë sisters</a>, Emily, Anne and Charlotte were born along with their brother Branwell at <a href="/wiki/Thornton,_West_Yorkshire" title="Thornton, West Yorkshire">74 Market Street in Thornton</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bradford" title="Bradford">Bradford</a> before moving to the <a href="/wiki/Bront%C3%AB_Parsonage_Museum" title="Brontë Parsonage Museum">parsonage</a> at <a href="/wiki/Haworth" title="Haworth">Haworth</a> in the heart of West Yorkshire's Brontë Country where they wrote a range of classics of English literature including "Wuthering Heights" and "Jane Eyre".
</p><p>The city played an important part in the early history of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>. A mural on the back of the Priestley Centre For The Arts in <a href="/wiki/Little_Germany,_Bradford" title="Little Germany, Bradford">Little Germany</a> commemorates the centenary of the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Labour_Party" title="Independent Labour Party">Independent Labour Party</a> in Bradford in 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Pals_battalions" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Pals battalions">The Bradford Pals</a> were three First World War Pals battalions of Kitchener's Army raised in the city. When the three battalions were taken over by the British Army they were officially named the 16th, 18th and 20th  Battalions, The Prince of Wales's Own West Yorkshire Regiment.
</p><p>On the morning of 1 July 1916, an estimated 1,394 young men from Bradford and District The Bradford Pals, the 16th and 18th Battalions of the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Regiment" title="West Yorkshire Regiment">Prince of Wales Own West Yorkshire Regiment</a> left their trenches in Northern France to advance across No Man's Land. It was the first hour of the first day of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Battle of the Somme</a>. Of the estimated 1,394 men who left the trenches 1,094 were either killed or injured during the ill-fated attack on the village of <a href="/wiki/Serre-l%C3%A8s-Puisieux" title="Serre-lès-Puisieux">Serre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other Bradford Battalions involved in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Battle of the Somme</a> were 1st/6th Territorial Battalion of The Prince of Wales's Own West Yorkshire Regiment, based at Belle Vue barracks in <a href="/wiki/Manningham,_Bradford" title="Manningham, Bradford">Manningham</a> and the 10th Battalion of The Prince of Wales's Own West Yorkshire Regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The 1st/6th Territorial Battalion of The Prince of Wales's Own West Yorkshire Regiment first saw action in 1915 at <a href="/wiki/Neuve_Chapelle" class="mw-redirect" title="Neuve Chapelle">Neuve Chapelle</a> before moving north to <a href="/wiki/Yser_Canal" class="mw-redirect" title="Yser Canal">Yser Canal</a> near Ypres.
The 10th Battalion The Prince of Wales's Own West Yorkshire Regiment was involved in the attack on <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Fricourt" title="Capture of Fricourt">Fricourt</a>, the 10th West Yorks suffered the highest casualty rate of any battalion on the Somme on 1 July and perhaps the highest battalion casualty list for a single day during the entire war. Nearly 60% of the battalion's casualties were deaths.
</p><p>In 1919 the Diocese of Bradford was founded, the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Cathedral" title="Bradford Cathedral">Church of Saint Peter</a> was then elevated to cathedral status.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg/250px-Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg/375px-Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg/500px-Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationalmediamuseum_02dec2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The National Science and Media Museum</div></div></div>
<p>The current city boundaries date from 1 April 1974, when the <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> of Bradford was merged with the borough of Keighley, the urban districts of <a href="/wiki/Baildon" title="Baildon">Baildon</a>, Bingley, Denholme, Ilkley, Shipley and Silsden, along with the <a href="/wiki/Queensbury,_West_Yorkshire" title="Queensbury, West Yorkshire">Queensbury</a> parts of <a href="/wiki/Queensbury_and_Shelf_Urban_District" title="Queensbury and Shelf Urban District">Queensbury and Shelf Urban District</a> and the parishes of <a href="/wiki/Addingham" title="Addingham">Addingham</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Steeton_with_Eastburn" title="Steeton with Eastburn">Steeton with Eastburn</a> from <a href="/wiki/Skipton_Rural_District" title="Skipton Rural District">Skipton Rural District</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kildwick" title="Kildwick">Kildwick</a> was part of Bradford at this time, but has since been moved into the Craven District (part of North Yorkshire).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Media_Museum" title="National Science and Media Museum">National Science and Media Museum</a> (formerly the National Museum of Photography, Film and Television) was established in the city in 1983. One of the first cinema shows outside London took place on the site where the museum now stands, in a music hall known as the People's Palace.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Today, the National Science and Media Museum hosts the annual Widescreen Weekend film festival.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With a large influx of South Asian immigrants and the local council's pursuit of a policy of <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multiculturalism</a> in the 1980s, separatism between ethnic communities became an issue.<sup id="cite_ref-taa_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taa-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 1989, a section of the Muslim community led a campaign against <a href="/wiki/Salman_Rushdie" title="Salman Rushdie">Salman Rushdie</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Satanic_Verses" title="The Satanic Verses">The Satanic Verses</a></i>, and caught the attention of the international media by publicly burning a copy of the book.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In July 2001, ethnic tensions led to <a href="/wiki/2001_Bradford_riots" title="2001 Bradford riots">rioting</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ouseley_Report" title="Ouseley Report">Ouseley Report</a>, written shortly before the riots broke out, noted that Bradford had become deeply divided by segregated schooling, with communities deeply ignorant of each other, and there was widespread fear of crime and violence which West Yorkshire Police had insufficiently tackled for fear of being branded racist.<sup id="cite_ref-taa_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taa-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In one case, a Bradford man whose car was set on fire following his conversion complained to police, but the officer advised him to "stop being a crusader and move to another place."<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response to the Ouseley Report, approximately £3 million was provided by the Home Office and the Neighbourhood Renewal Fund to regenerate the city.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> A further £2 billion was invested in regenerating the city centre, building a banqueting hall, new housing and leisure facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Saltaire_Salts_Mill_1.jpg" class="image" title="Salts Mill"><img alt="Salts Mill" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Saltaire_Salts_Mill_1.jpg/220px-Saltaire_Salts_Mill_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Saltaire_Salts_Mill_1.jpg/330px-Saltaire_Salts_Mill_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Saltaire_Salts_Mill_1.jpg/440px-Saltaire_Salts_Mill_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="865" /></a></div>
<p>In December 2001, <a href="/wiki/Saltaire" title="Saltaire">Saltaire</a> was designated a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>. This means that the government has a duty to protect the site. The buildings belonging to the model village are individually listed, with the highest level of protection given to the Congregational church (since 1972 known as the <a href="/wiki/United_Reformed_Church" title="United Reformed Church">United Reformed Church</a>) which is listed grade I. The village which includes <a href="/wiki/Salts_Mill" title="Salts Mill">Salts Mill</a> (pictured right) has survived remarkably complete with Roberts Park on the north side of the river recently restored by Bradford Council.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2007, Bradford was voted the greenest city in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-T&amp;A_Green_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T&amp;A_Green-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In the Sustainable Cities Index, compiled by <a href="/wiki/Forum_for_the_Future" title="Forum for the Future">Forum for the Future</a>, the city was revealed to have the lowest <a href="/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Environment (biophysical)">environmental</a> impact of any British city.<sup id="cite_ref-SCI2007_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCI2007-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In spite of its undeniably large role in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, Bradford's rivers were not polluted beyond redemption, and the streams surrounding the city are now a haven of <a href="/wiki/Wildlife" title="Wildlife">wildlife</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian2007_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2007-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The City of Bradford has areas of <a href="/wiki/Greenway_(landscape)" title="Greenway (landscape)">green space</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recycling</a> schemes.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradford became the world's first <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/City_of_Film" title="City of Film">City of Film</a> in 2009.
</p><p>The cinema connections in the city (which is also the home of the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Media_Museum" title="National Science and Media Museum">National Science and Media Museum</a>) are both historical and contemporary, with ongoing efforts to preserve, promote and enrich the city's heritage of film. Bradford has been a film location since the beginning of cinema, with its indigenous film industry being traced back to the years around the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>. By then the residents of Bradford had already witnessed important contributions to cinema development, such as the invention of the Cieroscope in <a href="/wiki/Manningham,_Bradford" title="Manningham, Bradford">Manningham</a> in 1896.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/City_of_Film" title="City of Film">City of Film</a> designation recognises Bradford's aim to use this history and the local popularity and accessibility of film as a major tool for regeneration, cultural development and social inclusion.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The City of Bradford is situated on the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a>, and is bounded to the east by the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Leeds" title="City of Leeds">City of Leeds</a>, the south east by the Metropolitan Borough of <a href="/wiki/Kirklees" title="Kirklees">Kirklees</a> and the south west by the Metropolitan Borough of <a href="/wiki/Calderdale" title="Calderdale">Calderdale</a>. The Lancashire borough of <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Pendle" title="Borough of Pendle">Pendle</a> lies to the west, whilst North Yorkshire boroughs of <a href="/wiki/Craven" title="Craven">Craven</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harrogate" title="Harrogate">Harrogate</a> lie to the north west and north east respectively. Bradford district has 3636&#160;hectares of upland heathland, including <a href="/wiki/Ilkley_Moor" title="Ilkley Moor">Ilkley Moor</a> where the peat bogs rise to 402&#160;m (1,319&#160;ft) above sea level. Less than 5% of the Bradford district is woodland. <a href="/wiki/Open_space_reserve" title="Open space reserve">Greenspace</a> accounts for 73.8% of the City of Bradford's total area, domestic buildings and gardens comprise 12.1%, and the rest is made up of roads and non-domestic buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Three river systems serve the City of Bradford, along with 23&#160;km of canal. The <a href="/wiki/Airedale" title="Airedale">Airedale</a> towns of Keighley, <a href="/wiki/Bingley" title="Bingley">Bingley</a> and Shipley lie on the <a href="/wiki/River_Aire" title="River Aire">River Aire</a>. The <a href="/wiki/River_Wharfe" title="River Wharfe">River Wharfe</a> runs through Ilkley and <a href="/wiki/Burley_in_Wharfedale" title="Burley in Wharfedale">Burley in Wharfedale</a>, and tributaries of the <a href="/wiki/River_Calder,_West_Yorkshire" title="River Calder, West Yorkshire">River Calder</a> run through the district. Unusually for a major settlement, Bradford is not built on any substantial body of water. The ford from which it takes its name (Broad-Ford) was a crossing of the stream called <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Beck" title="Bradford Beck">Bradford Beck</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parishes">Parishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Parishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While most of Bradford is <a href="/wiki/Civil_parishes_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil parishes in England">unparished</a>, there are parish and town councils for most of the outlying towns and villages in the District.  From 2009, the parishes are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Addingham" title="Addingham">Addingham</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baildon" title="Baildon">Baildon</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Burley_in_Wharfedale" title="Burley in Wharfedale">Burley</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clayton,_West_Yorkshire" title="Clayton, West Yorkshire">Clayton</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cullingworth" title="Cullingworth">Cullingworth</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Denholme" title="Denholme">Denholme</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harden,_West_Yorkshire" title="Harden, West Yorkshire">Harden</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haworth" title="Haworth">Haworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cross_Roads,_West_Yorkshire" title="Cross Roads, West Yorkshire">Cross Roads</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Stanbury" title="Stanbury">Stanbury</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ilkley" title="Ilkley">Ilkley</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Keighley" title="Keighley">Keighley</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Menston" title="Menston">Menston</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oxenhope" title="Oxenhope">Oxenhope</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sandy_Lane,_West_Yorkshire" title="Sandy Lane, West Yorkshire">Sandy Lane</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Silsden" title="Silsden">Silsden</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Steeton_with_Eastburn" title="Steeton with Eastburn">Steeton with Eastburn</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Trident,_West_Yorkshire" title="Trident, West Yorkshire">Trident</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wilsden" title="Wilsden">Wilsden</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wrose" title="Wrose">Wrose</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_City_Hall_025.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bradford_City_Hall_025.jpg/220px-Bradford_City_Hall_025.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bradford_City_Hall_025.jpg/330px-Bradford_City_Hall_025.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bradford_City_Hall_025.jpg/440px-Bradford_City_Hall_025.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2580" data-file-height="3524" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradford_City_Hall_025.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Hall" title="Bradford City Hall">Bradford City Hall</a> Tower and Flagpole</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliamentary_constituencies">Parliamentary constituencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Parliamentary constituencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2016</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The residents of Bradford are represented in the <a href="/wiki/British_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="British Parliament">British Parliament</a> by <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Members of Parliament</a> (MPs) for five separate parliamentary constituencies. <a href="/wiki/Bradford_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bradford East (UK Parliament constituency)">Bradford East</a> is represented by <a href="/wiki/Imran_Hussain_(British_politician)" title="Imran Hussain (British politician)">Imran Hussain</a> (Labour), <a href="/wiki/Bradford_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bradford West (UK Parliament constituency)">Bradford West</a> is represented by <a href="/wiki/Naz_Shah" title="Naz Shah">Naz Shah</a> (Labour), <a href="/wiki/Bradford_South_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bradford South (UK Parliament constituency)">Bradford South</a> is represented by <a href="/wiki/Judith_Cummins" title="Judith Cummins">Judith Cummins</a> (Labour),  <a href="/wiki/Shipley_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Shipley (UK Parliament constituency)">Shipley</a> is represented by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Davies" title="Philip Davies">Philip Davies</a> (Conservative), and
<a href="/wiki/Keighley_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Keighley (UK Parliament constituency)">Keighley</a> is represented by <a href="/wiki/John_Grogan_(British_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Grogan (British politician)">John Grogan</a> (Labour).
</p><p>The city played an important part in the early history of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>. A mural on the back of the Priestley Centre For The Arts (visible from Leeds Road) commemorates the centenary of the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Labour_Party" title="Independent Labour Party">Independent Labour Party</a> in 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradford is within the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Yorkshire and the Humber (European Parliament constituency)">Yorkshire and the Humber</a> European constituency, which is represented by two <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Independence_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Independence Party">UKIP</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a>, and two Labour <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEPs</a>. The voting figures for Bradford in the <a href="/wiki/2009_European_Parliament_election_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="2009 European Parliament election in the United Kingdom">European Parliament election</a> in June 2009 were: Conservative 24.7%, Labour 22.6%, UKIP 14.9%, Lib Dem 13.4%, BNP 9.4%, <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green</a> 8.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Council">Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/City_of_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council" title="City of Bradford Metropolitan District Council">City of Bradford Metropolitan District Council</a></div>
<p>In 1974, <a href="/wiki/City_Of_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="City Of Bradford Metropolitan District Council">City Of Bradford Metropolitan District Council</a> was created to administer the newly formed metropolitan borough. The county borough of Bradford was merged with the Borough of Keighley, the Urban Districts of Baildon, Bingley, <a href="/wiki/Cullingworth" title="Cullingworth">Cullingworth</a>, Denholme, Ilkley, Shipley and Silsden, along with part of <a href="/wiki/Queensbury_and_Shelf_Urban_District" title="Queensbury and Shelf Urban District">Queensbury and Shelf Urban District</a> and part of <a href="/wiki/Skipton_Rural_District" title="Skipton Rural District">Skipton Rural District</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">Local Government Act 1972</a>. The Council, which is based at <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Hall" title="Bradford City Hall">Bradford City Hall</a> in Centenary Square, governs the whole metropolitan district. The city was granted the right on 18 September 1907 to elect a <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayors_of_Bradford" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayors of Bradford">Lord Mayor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city is divided into 30 Electoral <a href="/wiki/Wards_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Wards of the United Kingdom">Wards</a>, each ward electing three <a href="/wiki/Councillor" title="Councillor">Councillors</a>. Elections are held in May, where one third of the 90 seats (one for each ward) are contested and the successful candidate is elected for a period of four years.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electoral_wards">Electoral wards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Electoral wards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Bradford_City_Council.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Coat_of_arms_of_Bradford_City_Council.png/220px-Coat_of_arms_of_Bradford_City_Council.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Coat_of_arms_of_Bradford_City_Council.png/330px-Coat_of_arms_of_Bradford_City_Council.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Coat_of_arms_of_Bradford_City_Council.png/440px-Coat_of_arms_of_Bradford_City_Council.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1377" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Bradford_City_Council.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bradford Coat of Arms</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Bradford" title="Coat of arms of Bradford">coat of arms of Bradford City council</a> is based on that of the former City and County Borough Council, with additions to indicate the merger of eleven Yorkshire councils.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The boar's head, as in the former city council's crest, refers to the legend of the boar of Cliffe Wood. This was a ferocious <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a> that terrorised the populace and caused much damage to land and property; so much so that the <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_the_Manor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord of the Manor">Lord of the Manor</a> offered a reward for anyone brave enough to slay the boar and bring its head to the Manor House. The mural crown is a frequent symbol of local government, but here also suggests a well head.<sup id="cite_ref-civicheraldry.co.uk_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civicheraldry.co.uk-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The stag is derived from the device of the Denholme Urban District Council and the arms of the former Borough of Keighley, but represents the District as a whole. The white <a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">angora goat</a> is retained from the former arms, recalling that the wool of this animal was used in the local industries. The roses on the collars refer to the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_rose" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire rose">Yorkshire rose</a> and the compartment resembles the area's hills and <a href="/wiki/Valley" title="Valley">dales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-civicheraldry.co.uk_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civicheraldry.co.uk-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The original Bradford Coat of Arms had the Latin words '<a href="/wiki/Labor_omnia_vincit" title="Labor omnia vincit">LABOR OMNIA VINCIT</a>' below it, meaning Work conquers all.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Bradford" title="Demography of Bradford">Demography of Bradford</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png/220px-Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png/330px-Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png/440px-Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png 2x" data-file-width="18266" data-file-height="17494" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_Density_Bradford_Metropolitan_District_Council_Area_2011_Census.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population density in the Bradford Metropolitan District Council Area from the 2011 census<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>At the 2011 UK census, the City of Bradford had a population of 522,452.<sup id="cite_ref-bradford.gov.uk_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bradford.gov.uk-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Of the 180,246 <a href="/wiki/Household" title="Household">households</a> in Bradford, 36.5% were <a href="/wiki/Married" class="mw-redirect" title="Married">married</a> couples living together, 28% were one-person households, 10.8% were <a href="/wiki/Single-parent" class="mw-redirect" title="Single-parent">lone parents</a> and 8.4% were <a href="/wiki/Cohabitation" title="Cohabitation">co-habiting</a> couples, following a similar trend to the rest of England.<sup id="cite_ref-statistics.gov.uk_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics.gov.uk-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 1,290 inhabitants per square kilometre (3,341/sq mi) and for every 100 females, there were 92.8 males. Of those aged 16–74, 24.5% had no academic qualifications, lower than the 28.9% in all of England. 11.8% of Bradford residents were born outside the United Kingdom, higher than the England average of 9.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-statistics.gov.uk_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics.gov.uk-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2011 census, it stated that 67.44% (352,317) of the city's population was White (All White ethnic groups), 2.48% (12,979) (Mixed ethnic groups), 26.83% (140,149) (All Asian ethnic groups), 1.77% (9,267) (All Black ethnic groups) and 1.48% (7,740) (all other ethnic groups).<sup id="cite_ref-bradford.gov.uk_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bradford.gov.uk-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The ONS Regional Trends report, published in June 2009, showed that most of the urban core<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> and 41% of the district as a whole were among the most deprived in the country, it also showed that 11% of the district as a whole were among the least deprived in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Bradford has one of the highest unemployment rates in England,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> with the economic inactivity rates of Black, Asian and Minority Ethnic groups standing at over 50% of the working age population.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The crime rate in the City of Bradford is significantly higher than the national average,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> but lower than that of similar cities such as <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/City_of_Leeds" title="City of Leeds">Leeds</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bronte_Parsonage_Museum.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bronte_Parsonage_Museum.JPG/300px-Bronte_Parsonage_Museum.JPG" decoding="async" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bronte_Parsonage_Museum.JPG/450px-Bronte_Parsonage_Museum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Bronte_Parsonage_Museum.JPG/600px-Bronte_Parsonage_Museum.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bronte_Parsonage_Museum.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center><a href="/wiki/Bront%C3%AB_Parsonage_Museum" title="Brontë Parsonage Museum">Brontë Parsonage Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haworth" title="Haworth">Haworth</a></center></div></div></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Bront%C3%AB_Country" title="Brontë Country">Brontë Country</a></i> is an area including Western parts of the City as well as the area to the west. The City of Bradford includes the town of <a href="/wiki/Haworth" title="Haworth">Haworth</a> and the village of <a href="/wiki/Thornton,_West_Yorkshire" title="Thornton, West Yorkshire">Thornton</a>, the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Bront%C3%AB_family" title="Brontë family">Brontë sisters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Keighley_and_Worth_Valley_Railway" title="Keighley and Worth Valley Railway">Keighley and Worth Valley Railway</a>, Ilkley's <a href="/wiki/Cow_and_Calf_Rocks" class="mw-redirect" title="Cow and Calf Rocks">Cow and Calf Rocks</a>, Bradford's <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Media_Museum" title="National Science and Media Museum">National Science and Media Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Park" title="Bradford City Park">Bradford City Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cartwright_Hall" title="Cartwright Hall">Cartwright Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saltaire" title="Saltaire">Saltaire</a> village (a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Salts_Mill" title="Salts Mill">Salts Mill</a> are key attractions that draw visitors from across the globe.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The City of Bradford has also become the first <a href="/wiki/City_of_Film" title="City of Film">UNESCO City of Film</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Annual events such as the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Literature_Festival" title="Bradford Literature Festival">Bradford Literature Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Film_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Bradford Film Festival">Bradford Film Festival</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bradfordfestival.org.uk/">Bradford Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_Park" title="Bradford City Park">Bradford Mela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bingley_Music_Live" title="Bingley Music Live">Bingley Music Live</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilkley_Literature_Festival" title="Ilkley Literature Festival">Ilkley Literature Festival</a>, Haworth's 1940s weekend, <a href="/wiki/Saltaire_Festival" title="Saltaire Festival">Saltaire Festival</a> and special Christmas events take place across the district.
</p><p>The value of tourism to the district's economy stands at more than £500 million a year, with an estimated 8.6 million day trips within the district. The impact of this is more than 13,500 jobs supported by the tourism and retail sector.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_Bradford" title="List of companies based in Bradford">List of companies based in Bradford</a></div>
<p>The economy of Bradford is worth around <a href="/wiki/List_of_UK_cities_by_GVA" title="List of UK cities by GVA">£9.5</a> billion, contributing around 8.4% of <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="Yorkshire and the Humber">the region's</a> output, and making the district the third largest after <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a> in Yorkshire &amp; Humber.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Traditionally based on the wool and <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textile</a> industries, manufacturing is still strong, accounting for around 1 in 5 jobs. The city's service-sector economy accounts for 77% of the district's 195,000 jobs, with today's fastest-growing sectors including <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retail</a> headquarters and distribution.<sup id="cite_ref-yorkshire-forward.com_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yorkshire-forward.com-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The district is home to a number of large businesses with recognised brands operating on a national and international scale such as <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Morrisons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pace_plc" title="Pace plc">Pace Plc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hallmark_Cards" title="Hallmark Cards">Hallmark Cards</a>. Three of the UK's biggest financial institutions are based in Bradford: <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Building_Society" title="Yorkshire Building Society">Yorkshire Building Society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santander_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander Group">Santander Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Provident_Financial" title="Provident Financial">Provident Financial</a>. It is also home to nationally outstanding cultural businesses, a strong group of new media companies, and a significant national institution in the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_and_Media_Museum" title="National Science and Media Museum">National Science and Media Museum</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">Tourism</a> is worth over £400 million to the local economy, and employs over 10,000 people. Bradford's <a href="/wiki/Exports" class="mw-redirect" title="Exports">exports</a> are worth almost £700&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-yorkshire-forward.com_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yorkshire-forward.com-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city's working-age population has risen by 3.3% since 2000, faster than any UK city outside London, whilst the population of the city itself is growing by twice the national average. Bradford has a younger age profile than the Yorkshire &amp; Humber regional average and the national average, with the younger age groups forming a greater proportion of the population in comparison.<sup id="cite_ref-bradfordeconomy1_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bradfordeconomy1-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Bradford has been named by research group OMIS as one of the top six cities in the UK equipped for future growth, and the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_British_Industry" title="Confederation of British Industry">CBI</a> reports that <a href="/wiki/Business_confidence" class="mw-redirect" title="Business confidence">business confidence</a> is higher in Bradford than in the UK as a whole, whilst £1.5&#160;billion of construction work is transforming Bradford in a bid to attract further investment.<sup id="cite_ref-yorkshire-forward.com_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yorkshire-forward.com-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the 2001 UK census, Bradford had 326,774 residents aged 16 to 74. 2.5% of these people were students with jobs, 7.6% looking after home or family, 6.1% permanently sick or disabled and 4.5% economically inactive for other reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The City of Bradford has a lower economic activity rate than West Yorkshire, the regional average for Yorkshire and the Humber and the national average. Conversely Bradford has a higher economic inactivity rate than all these areas and also has a lower employment rate.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">Manufacturing</a> is still strong in Bradford and accounts for almost 12% of all jobs, and the city's service-sector economy accounts for 82% of the district's 192,000 jobs. The <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurial_mindset" class="mw-redirect" title="Entrepreneurial mindset">entrepreneurial spirit</a> is more present in Bradford than generally in the UK, with start-ups accounting for 12% of the business community.<sup id="cite_ref-yorkshire-forward.com_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yorkshire-forward.com-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bradford's <a href="/wiki/Gross_value_added" title="Gross value added">GVA</a> is over £6&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-yorkshire-forward.com_83-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yorkshire-forward.com-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Education in the city is provided for by <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Bradford" title="List of schools in Bradford">a number of schools and colleges</a>. State schooling is managed by Bradford <a href="/wiki/Local_education_authority" title="Local education authority">local education authority</a>. There are also a number of independent (private) and free schools, such as <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Grammar_School" title="Bradford Grammar School">Bradford Grammar School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Woodhouse_Grove_School" title="Woodhouse Grove School">Woodhouse Grove School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Girls_Grammar_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Bradford Girls Grammar School">Bradford Girls Grammar School</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bradford_College_(England)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bradford College (England)">Bradford College</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bradford" title="University of Bradford">University of Bradford</a> are the main further and higher education providers.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Public transport in Bradford is co-ordinated by <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Metro" title="West Yorkshire Metro">Metro</a>. Most local train services are run by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>, with longer-distance services to <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross railway station</a> served by <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_(train_operating_company)" title="Grand Central (train operating company)">Grand Central</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Interchange" title="Bradford Interchange">Bradford Interchange</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Forster_Square_railway_station" title="Bradford Forster Square railway station">Bradford Forster Square station</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Wharfedale_line" title="Wharfedale line">Wharfedale line</a> connects direct to <a href="/wiki/Ilkley_railway_station" title="Ilkley railway station">Ilkley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Rhydding_railway_station" title="Ben Rhydding railway station">Ben Rhydding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burley-in-Wharfedale_railway_station" title="Burley-in-Wharfedale railway station">Burley-in-Wharfedale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Menston_railway_station" title="Menston railway station">Menston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guiseley_railway_station" title="Guiseley railway station">Guiseley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baildon_railway_station" title="Baildon railway station">Baildon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shipley_railway_station" title="Shipley railway station">Shipley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frizinghall_railway_station" title="Frizinghall railway station">Frizinghall</a> railway stations with <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Forster_Square_railway_station" title="Bradford Forster Square railway station">Bradford Forster Square</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Airedale_line" title="Airedale line">Airedale line</a> connects the stations at <a href="/wiki/Morecambe_railway_station" title="Morecambe railway station">Morecambe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_railway_station" title="Lancaster railway station">Lancaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Settle_railway_station" title="Settle railway station">Settle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_railway_station" title="Carlisle railway station">Carlisle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skipton_railway_station" title="Skipton railway station">Skipton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steeton_and_Silsden_railway_station" title="Steeton and Silsden railway station">Steeton and Silsden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keighley_railway_station" title="Keighley railway station">Keighley</a> (change for the <a href="/wiki/Bront%C3%AB_Country" title="Brontë Country">Brontë Country</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Worth_Valley_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Worth Valley Railway">Worth Valley Railway</a>), <a href="/wiki/Crossflatts_railway_station" title="Crossflatts railway station">Crossflatts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bingley_railway_station" title="Bingley railway station">Bingley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saltaire_railway_station" title="Saltaire railway station">Saltaire</a> (<a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Shipley_railway_station" title="Shipley railway station">Shipley</a>, continuing to either <a href="/wiki/Frizinghall_railway_station" title="Frizinghall railway station">Frizinghall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Forster_Square_railway_station" title="Bradford Forster Square railway station">Bradford Forster Square</a> or to <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a> to the east of the district. Both <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Forster_Square_railway_station" title="Bradford Forster Square railway station">Bradford Forster Square</a> and the districts major and busiest railway station <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Interchange" title="Bradford Interchange">Bradford Interchange</a> are served by the <a href="/wiki/Leeds%E2%80%93Bradford_lines" title="Leeds–Bradford lines">Leeds–Bradford lines</a> with direct routes to Leeds, <a href="/wiki/Selby_railway_station" title="Selby railway station">Selby</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Interchange" title="Bradford Interchange">Bradford Interchange</a>, via the <a href="/wiki/Calder_Valley_line" title="Calder Valley line">Calder Valley line</a>, also connects direct to stations at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_station" title="Manchester Victoria station">Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halifax_railway_station_(West_Yorkshire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Halifax railway station (West Yorkshire)">Halifax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rochdale_railway_station" title="Rochdale railway station">Rochdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burnley_Manchester_Road_railway_station" title="Burnley Manchester Road railway station">Burnley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_railway_station" title="Blackburn railway station">Blackburn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preston_railway_station" title="Preston railway station">Preston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poulton-le-Fylde_railway_station" title="Poulton-le-Fylde railway station">Poulton-le-Fylde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_North_railway_station" title="Blackpool North railway station">Blackpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Westgate_railway_station" title="Wakefield Westgate railway station">Wakefield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_railway_station" title="Doncaster railway station">Doncaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chester" title="Chester">Chester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warrington" title="Warrington">Warrington</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London</a>.
</p><p>There are bus stations in Bradford, Ilkley, Keighley and Shipley. The majority of services are provided by <a href="/wiki/First_Bradford" title="First Bradford">First Bradford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keighley_Bus_Company" title="Keighley Bus Company">Keighley Bus Company</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/M606_motorway" title="M606 motorway">M606</a>, a spur off the <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62 motorway</a>, connects the district with the national motorway network. The <a href="/wiki/M606_motorway" title="M606 motorway">M606</a> was originally laid out to reach the centre of Bradford and beyond, but connects instead to the <a href="/wiki/A6177_road" title="A6177 road">A6177</a> Bradford outer ring road, making the motorway one of the shortest in the country at less than three miles (5&#160;km) long. Another motorway was planned in the 1970s, envisaging a link between Bradford, the Aire valley in the north of the district and the <a href="/wiki/M65_motorway" title="M65 motorway">M65</a> at Colne, roughly mirroring the existing <a href="/wiki/A650_road" title="A650 road">A650 road</a>. It has since been upgraded to dual carriageway along much of its length, bypassing the towns of Bingley and Keighley. The <a href="/wiki/A658_road" title="A658 road">A658 road</a> passes through a tunnel underneath the main <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bradford_Airport" title="Leeds Bradford Airport">Leeds Bradford Airport</a> runway as it heads north-east from Bradford to <a href="/wiki/Knaresborough" title="Knaresborough">Knaresborough</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bradford_Airport" title="Leeds Bradford Airport">Leeds Bradford Airport</a> itself is located in <a href="/wiki/Yeadon,_West_Yorkshire" title="Yeadon, West Yorkshire">Yeadon</a>, about 10 miles (16&#160;km) to the north-east of the city centre, and has both charter and scheduled flights to destinations within Europe plus the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.  There are connections to the rest of the world via <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris-Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris-Charles de Gaulle Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a>.
</p><p>There are also <a href="/wiki/Navigable_waterway" class="mw-redirect" title="Navigable waterway">navigable waterways</a> that run through the district. The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Liverpool_Canal" title="Leeds and Liverpool Canal">Leeds and Liverpool Canal</a> passes through numerous towns and villages in the borough, with the Grade I listed <a href="/wiki/Bingley_Five_Rise_Locks" title="Bingley Five Rise Locks">Five Rise Locks</a> at Bingley generally considered to be one of the finest
feats of canal engineering in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> There are also proposals to restore and re-open the <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Canal" title="Bradford Canal">Bradford Canal</a>, which closed in 1922, as part of a wider regeneration of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns">Twin towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=City_of_Bradford&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Twin towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The City of Bradford, and the various towns and villages that make up the Metropolitan District, have Twin Town and Sister City Friendship Agreements with several other communities.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Each was originally twinned with a place within the City of Bradford.
</p>
